| 1:52:53| So, here's how that process works. And I will respectfully disagree with George in that there is a classification plan and a compensation plan.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6773)|
| 1:53:04| In the HR profession, you have a class listing, and that's going to list  that's going to house your job classifications and those specifications and descriptions.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6784)|
| 1:53:14| You're also going to have a salary structure. The combination of those two things is your class comp plan. It is one plan, and they do work like this.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6794)|
| 1:53:23| That's what we bring to council. Job classifications don't come to council. That would wear you out if we had to bring those every time we changed or amended a new job description.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6803)|
| 1:53:34| What comes to council is the class comp plan, which is a single plan, and it's where you intermarry all of your job classifications with your three salary structures.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6814)|
| 1:53:45| The way that we monitor that and make amendments to that, we do collect data. Even in years we don't do a comprehensive survey, we're always collecting data.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6825)|

| 1:54:16| So, we do that regularly. | 1:54:30| In the years we've hired a consultant, I work closely with the consultant. We basically do the survey together, and they don't just do a survey and hand us a product.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6870)|
| 1:54:40| Even in those years, we're working with them on every single step. We help them design the survey. We help them look at the data. We work on every piece of that.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6880)|
| 1:54:50| So, when we finish that process, I then look at it initially for recommendations under the classification compensation plan.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6890)|
| 1:54:59| Do our structures themselves need upward adjustments to better reflect market rates? Do individual job classes need to be readjusted? Do they need to be in a different pay grade? Do they need a better job title?| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6899)|
| 1:55:12| That's why I say it's a class comp plan. The whole thing works as one.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6912)|
| 1:55:16| Once I take a look at that and determine some initial recommendations based on my experience doing those, I then sit down with the finance director.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6916)|
| 1:55:27| That's usually step one because I want to say, here's what it looks like we need to do, and this is what we've done. I've been doing this for the city for 15 years, this part.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6927)|
| 1:55:38| Every year, I sit down with the finance director, usually in February. I go through what, based on the data, look like the ideal recommendations. If we could have our wish list, here's what we need to do.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6938)|
| 1:55:51| Then the finance director and I work on those together to ensure that they're going to be agreeable with the budget.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6951)|
| 1:55:58| Sometimes it's something that our wish list, we simply can't afford to do it. We look at that together at that point and work on a final set of recommendations that meet our best needs, most important needs, and still come in with responsible budget considerations.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6958)|
| 1:56:15| Once the finance director and I have something that we both feel meets the class comp needs and the budget needs, we establish a meeting with the mayor. We sit down and propose our joint recommendations to the mayor.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6975)|
| 1:56:30| In past years, usually it's a couple of meetings to ensure that the mayor has any data that she needs, understands the recommendations, has an opportunity to ask any questions.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=6990)|
| 1:56:44| It's always been a very cooperative, collaborative process. Once the mayor has had an opportunity to understand, review the recommendations, in my 15 years, I've only had one instance where the mayor wanted different recommendations.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7004)|
| 1:57:01| That was last year with the 7.7% increase for police. That was the only time in my tenure we have not arrived at a general consensus. That was just a last minute change that was inserted into it.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7021)|
| 1:57:18| Usually it's a collaborative process. We all are in agreement before that ordinance is even drafted and goes forward. But it is at the mayor's prerogative to add to those recommendations if the mayor feels there's something that is a priority or she wants to add an increase across the board.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7038)|
| 1:57:39| Certainly, the mayor then can ask me to add those into the class comp ordinance.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7059)|
| 1:57:45| Okay, thanks. So you bring a recommendation and you come to a consensus. It's not something that you come to within the Civil Service Merit Board.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7065)|
| 1:57:55| Correct.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7075)|
| 1:57:56| Thank you.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7076)|
| 1:57:59| Mr. Shields.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7079)|
| 1:58:02| Thank you, Vice Mayor. I just wanted to correct. It may be Civil Service's practice to treat classification as compensation as though they are too intertwined to be thought of as separate.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7082)|
| 1:58:14| But that's not what our charter says. Our charter treats them as separate. And that's important because, again, going back to when we had a personnel department and we had a Civil Service Merit Board, all under this charter that we're operating under now,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7094)|
| 1:58:28| it was recognized that compensation was the function of the personnel department and the mayor and finance alone.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7108)|
| 1:58:36| But classification was different because that does impact, you know, the fairness of the task you're assigned to do and the nature of your work.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7116)|
| 1:58:44| And so it was recognized then that the Merit Board had a role in monitoring classification to make sure that those merit system principles were being followed.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7124)|
| 1:58:52| Compensation is a budget process, and that's why the personnel department managed that process when we formally had it.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/city-council-ws-r-3877-200416?start=7132)|
